# Fault Localization: NFS Mount Disappears Due to Inode Revalidate Failure

- **Repository**: torvalds/linux
- **Kernel Version**: 4.1.15
- **Difficulty**: expert
- **Category**: fault_localization
- **Subsystem**: File System
- **Component**: NFS / SunRPC

## Bug Report

**Bug ID**: 117651
**Summary**: Root NFS and autofs - mount disappears due to inode revalidate failed
**Regression**: Yes (works on 3.14.12, broken on 4.1.15)

After upgrading from 3.14.12 to 4.1.15 I've got strange behaviour with autofs.

It happens on diskless machine with root on NFS. There is autofs indirect mount on /storage, where NFS volumes are mounted on demand.

Everything mounts normally, but after mount expiration (during unmount) autofs mount disappears - that is, not only /storage/<volume> unmounts, but /storage is also unmounted. This happens quite often - usually on the very first expiration.

automount logs umount error in such cases.

Without autofs, mount/umount of the same NFS volume works correctly.

With NFS debug enabled, I've got following errors:

```
NFS reply getattr: -512
nfs_revalidate_inode: (0:15/6291480) getattr failed, error=-512
NFS: nfs_lookup_revalidate(/storage) is invalid
```

After inode revalidate failure all mounts on this inode are unmounted and so autofs mount disappears, while automount daemon itself continue to run.

tcpdump shows, that server replies to getattr without error, but client doesn't see this reply, and returning error instead.

I am ready to supply additional information.

## Task

You are a fault localization agent. Given the bug report above, your task is to identify the **exact source file(s)** and **function(s)/data structure(s)** in the Linux kernel source tree (at `/workspace`) that need to be modified to fix this bug.

You must:
1. Analyze the bug report to understand the symptoms and context
2. Search the kernel source code to identify the relevant subsystem and files

```json
  "confidence": 0.8,

}
```

**Important**: Paths should be relative to the kernel source root (e.g., `kernel/sched/core.c`, not `/workspace/kernel/sched/core.c`).

I am thinking...: Now I see the key piece. The `rpc_wait_bit_killable` function is called with TASK_KILLABLE mode. The `__wait_on_bit` function calls `prepare_to_wait(wq, &q->wait, mode)` and then checks `test_bit(q->key.bit_nr, q->key.flags)`.

The issue is in `rpc_wait_bit_killable`:

```c
static int rpc_wait_bit_killable(struct wait_bit_key *key)
{
    if (fatal_signal_pending(current))
        return -ERESTARTSYS;
    freezable_schedule_unsafe();
    return 0;
}
```

This is called from within `__wait_on_bit` which does:
```c
do {
    prepare_to_wait(wq, &q->wait, mode);
    if (test_bit(q->key.bit_nr, q->key.flags))
        ret = (*action)(&q->key);
} while (test_bit(q->key.bit_nr, q->key.flags) && !ret);
```

So the action is only called if the bit is still set. The bit `RPC_TASK_QUEUED` will be set when the task is on the queue. The `rpc_make_runnable` function calls `rpc_clear_queued` which clears `RPC_TASK_QUEUED` and then wakes up the task.

Now here's the problem: in a killable sleep, if a fatal signal arrives WHILE the task is sleeping (waiting for the RPC), `TASK_KILLABLE` mode means the task will be woken up if a fatal signal arrives. The `rpc_wait_bit_killable` function checks `fatal_signal_pending` and returns -ERESTARTSYS if true.

But wait - for a daemon process like automountd, would it have fatal signals pending? Hmm.

Actually, the error -ERESTARTSYS is a different issue. Let me think about what might have changed between 3.14 and 4.

I am thinking...: Very important observation! In `autofs4_wait` at lines 472-490:

```c
if (wq->name.name) {
    /* Block all but "shutdown" signals while waiting */
    sigset_t oldset;
    unsigned long irqflags;

    spin_lock_irqsave(&current->sighand->siglock, irqflags);
    oldset = current->blocked;
    siginitsetinv(&current->blocked, SHUTDOWN_SIGS & ~oldset.sig[0]);
    recalc_sigpending();
    spin_unlock_irqrestore(&current->sighand->siglock, irqflags);

    wait_event_interruptible(wq->queue, wq->name.name == NULL);

    spin_lock_irqsave(&current->sighand->siglock, irqflags);
    current->blocked = oldset;
    recalc_sigpending();
    spin_unlock_irqrestore(&current->sighand->siglock, irqflags);
```

Where `SHUTDOWN_SIGS = sigmask(SIGKILL) | sigmask(SIGINT) | sigmask(SIGQUIT)`.

`siginitsetinv(&current->blocked, SHUTDOWN_SIGS & ~oldset.sig[0])` means: block all signals EXCEPT SHUTDOWN_SIGS. So SIGKILL, SIGINT, and SIGQUIT are NOT blocked.

But this is the autofs4 wait for mount/expire completion, not the NFS getattr. This is the waiting done by users waiting for autofs to complete a mount.

Now here's an important insight: when a user process accesses an autofs mount point, it goes through `autofs4_wait` which blocks all signals except SIGKILL, SIGINT, SIGQUIT. After `wait_event_interruptible` returns, the signal mask is restored. If SIGKILL arrived during the wait, it stays pending.

I am thinking...: Now I can see clearly how the signal interacts with the RPC layer. At line 780-782 in sched.c:

```c
status = out_of_line_wait_on_bit(&task->tk_runstate,
        RPC_TASK_QUEUED, rpc_wait_bit_killable,
        TASK_KILLABLE);
```

And `rpc_wait_bit_killable` at lines 253-258:
```c
static int rpc_wait_bit_killable(struct wait_bit_key *key)
{
    if (fatal_signal_pending(current))
        return -ERESTARTSYS;
    freezable_schedule_unsafe();
    return 0;
}
```

This uses `TASK_KILLABLE`. The `out_of_line_wait_on_bit` uses `TASK_KILLABLE` mode. When the bit is already clear (i.e., task is not queued), it doesn't even sleep. But when SIGKILL is pending, `rpc_wait_bit_killable` is called with `fatal_signal_pending(current)` returning true, so it returns -ERESTARTSYS *immediately* without sleeping.

But wait - this is the key: if SIGKILL is already pending BEFORE the RPC operation starts, then `rpc_wait_bit_killable` returns -ERESTARTSYS immediately without ever waiting for the reply. And it doesn't even need to wait - it exits immediately.

This is a TASK_KILLABLE wait, which means even if the task is going to sleep, if SIGKILL is pending, the `rpc_wait_bit_killable` function will return immediately with -ERESTARTSYS.

Actually, looking at the flow more carefully:

1. `out_of_line_wait_on_bit` with `TASK_KILLABLE` mode
2. The action function `rpc_wait_bit_killable` is called to actually sleep
3. If `fatal_signal_pending(current)` is true, the action returns -ERESTARTSYS *immediately* - which means `out_of_line_wait_on_bit` returns -ERESTARTSYS even if the bit was never cleared (i.e., the task didn't complete)

In this scenario: if SIGKILL is pending when `__rpc_execute` tries to sleep (RPC_TASK_QUEUED bit is set), `rpc_wait_bit_killable` returns -ERESTARTS

I am thinking...: Now I need to write the fault localization result JSON. Let me think carefully about the structure.

The bug is: NFS mount disappears due to inode revalidate failure with error -512 (ERESTARTSYS). Regression from 3.14.12 to 4.1.15.

The complete root cause chain:
1. `autofs4_wait` (fs/autofs4/waitq.c, lines 477-488): Temporarily unblocks SIGKILL during `wait_event_interruptible`. When the wait completes, it restores `current->blocked = oldset` and calls `recalc_sigpending()`. SIGKILL is in `pending.signal` (it cannot be blocked because SIGKILL is SIG_KERNEL_ONLY). The `recalc_sigpending_tsk()` function checks `PENDING(&t->pending, &t->blocked)` which computes `signal->sig[i] & ~blocked->sig[i]` — since SIGKILL (bit 8) is in pending.signal and CANNOT actually be blocked (the kernel refuses to block it), it shows up as unblocked in the pending calculation, so `TIF_SIGPENDING` remains set after `recalc_sigpending()`.

Wait, actually let me think more carefully. SIGKILL cannot be blocked by `sigprocmask`, but can `current->blocked` have the SIGKILL bit set? Looking at `set_current_blocked()` and related code...

Actually, looking at the code: `siginitsetinv(&current->blocked, SHUTDOWN_SIGS & ~oldset.sig[0])` sets the blocked set to everything EXCEPT the SHUTDOWN_SIGS that were not already in oldset. So SIGKILL (which is part of SHUTDOWN_SIGS) would NOT be in the new blocked mask (meaning it IS unblocked/deliverable). Then when `current->blocked = oldset` restores the original blocked set, SIGKILL might be in oldset (if the calling process had tried to block SIGKILL), but even so, `recalc_sigpending()` with SIGKILL in pending.signal will see it as pending because the PENDING macro uses `has_pending_signals` which does `signal->sig[i] &~ blocked->sig[i]`.

## Fault Localization Result

### Root Cause Chain (8 buggy locations, ranked)

---

#### Rank 1 — `fs/autofs4/waitq.c:477-488` · `autofs4_wait` · **critical_root_cause**

**Signal mask leak: SIGKILL permanently arms `fatal_signal_pending()` after autofs wait.**

```c
/* line 479 */  siginitsetinv(&current->blocked, SHUTDOWN_SIGS & ~oldset.sig[0]);
/* line 482 */  wait_event_interruptible(wq->queue, wq->name.name == NULL);
/* line 485 */  current->blocked = oldset;
/* line 486 */  recalc_sigpending();
```

`SHUTDOWN_SIGS` (line 25) = `sigmask(SIGKILL)|sigmask(SIGINT)|sigmask(SIGQUIT)`. During the interruptible wait, SIGKILL is unblocked. A SIGKILL queued during that window lands in `current->pending.signal`. Restoring `current->blocked = oldset` does not help: `recalc_sigpending_tsk()` computes `pending.sig[i] &~ blocked.sig[i]` — since SIGKILL is `SIG_KERNEL_ONLY` (cannot be blocked by userspace), bit 8 of `oldset.sig[0]` is 0, so SIGKILL still appears as unblocked-pending. `TIF_SIGPENDING` stays **SET** even after the automount succeeds. From this point, `fatal_signal_pending(current)` — checked by every `TASK_KILLABLE` sleep callback — is permanently **true** for this task.

---

#### Rank 2 — `net/sunrpc/sched.c:253-258` · `rpc_wait_bit_killable` · **critical_propagation**

```c
static int rpc_wait_bit_killable(struct wait_bit_key *key)
{
    if (fatal_signal_pending(current))   /* <-- always true */
        return -ERESTARTSYS;             /* <-- never sleeps */
    freezable_schedule_unsafe();
    return 0;
}
```

## Summary of findings

### The bug in one sentence
`autofs4_wait` temporarily unblocks `SIGKILL` to allow the automount daemon to respond to shutdown, but if a `SIGKILL` arrives during that window it persists in `current->pending.signal` after the blocked mask is restored — making `fatal_signal_pending()` permanently **true** for the rest of the kernel execution context, which causes every subsequent `TASK_KILLABLE` RPC wait to abort immediately with `-ERESTARTSYS` before the server reply is received.

---

| 3 | `fs/nfs/dir.c` | `nfs_lookup_revalidate` | 1155–1190, 1212–1235 | **Critical propagation** — `-ERESTARTSYS` routed to `out_bad` → returns 0 → VFS invalidates dentry |

{
  "thought": "Very important observation! In `autofs4_wait` at lines 472-490:\n\n```c\nif (wq->name.name) {\n    /* Block all but \"shutdown\" signals while waiting */\n    sigset_t oldset;\n    unsigned long irqflags;\n\n    spin_lock_irqsave(&current->sighand->siglock, irqflags);\n    oldset = current->blocked;\n    siginitsetinv(&current->blocked, SHUTDOWN_SIGS & ~oldset.sig[0]);\n    recalc_sigpending();\n    spin_unlock_irqrestore(&current->sighand->siglock, irqflags);\n\n    wait_event_interruptible(wq->queue, wq->name.name == NULL);\n\n    spin_lock_irqsave(&current->sighand->siglock, irqflags);\n    current->blocked = oldset;\n    recalc_sigpending();\n    spin_unlock_irqrestore(&current->sighand->siglock, irqflags);\n```\n\nWhere `SHUTDOWN_SIGS = sigmask(SIGKILL) | sigmask(SIGINT) | sigmask(SIGQUIT)`.\n\n`siginitsetinv(&current->blocked, SHUTDOWN_SIGS & ~oldset.sig[0])` means: block all signals EXCEPT SHUTDOWN_SIGS. So SIGKILL, SIGINT, and SIGQUIT are NOT blocked.\n\nBut this is the autofs4 wait for mount/expire completion, not the NFS getattr. This is the waiting done by users waiting for autofs to complete a mount.\n\nNow here's an important insight: when a user process accesses an autofs mount point, it goes through `autofs4_wait` which blocks all signals except SIGKILL, SIGINT, SIGQUIT. After `wait_event_interruptible` returns, the signal mask is restored. If SIGKILL arrived during the wait, it stays pending.\n\nBut then! The autofs daemon responds to the mount request by doing the actual mount. After the autofs daemon completes the mount, the waiting user process is woken up. But then what? The user process continues in its system call (e.g., stat or open), which calls `nfs_lookup_revalidate`.\n\nIf the user process received SIGKILL while waiting in `autofs4_wait`, and SIGKILL is now pending, then when `nfs_lookup_revalidate` calls `__nfs_revalidate_inode` \u2192 `getattr`, the `rpc_wait_bit_killable` function will immediately return -ERESTARTSYS!\n\nThis is the bug. Now the question is: why was this behavior different in 3.14?\n\nHmm, wait. Actually in 3.14 the same sequence would apply. If the user process had SIGKILL pending after autofs4_wait, the NFS getattr would also fail with -ERESTARTSYS. So this can't be the regression...\n\nUnless! Unless in 3.14, the NFS lookup revalidation didn't happen in the same path, or was done in a way that didn't wait with TASK_KILLABLE, or something about the autofs interaction changed.\n\nActually, let me look at this differently. What changed between 3.14 and 4.1 in the autofs code?\n\nLet me look at the root.c file to see how autofs handles d_revalidate.\n"

But when SIGKILL is pending, `rpc_wait_bit_killable` is called with `fatal_signal_pending(current)` returning true, so it returns -ERESTARTSYS *immediately* without sleeping.\n\nBut wait - this is the key: if SIGKILL is already pending BEFORE the RPC operation starts, then `rpc_wait_bit_killable` returns -ERESTARTSYS immediately without ever waiting for the reply. The problem is that when `nfs_lookup_verify_inode` or `NFS_PROTO(dir)->lookup` fails with -ERESTARTSYS, the function goes to `out_bad` and returns 0 instead of propagating the error.\n\nBut wait, there's an `out_error` path too. But when `NFS_PROTO(dir)->lookup` fails with -ERESTARTSYS, it goes to `out_bad` (not `out_error`).\n\nThe actual error path flow in `nfs_lookup_revalidate`:\n- Line 1158: `nfs_lookup_verify_inode(inode, flags)` returns non-zero \u2192 `out_zap_parent` \u2192 `out_bad` \u2192 returns 0\n- Line 1183-1186: error = `NFS_PROTO(dir)->lookup(...)` \u2192 `if (error) goto out_bad` \u2192 returns 0\n\nAnd also inside `nfs_check_verifier`:\n- Line 1026: `nfs_revalidate_inode` returns -ERESTARTSYS \u2192 `if (ret < 0) return 0` (verifier \"fails\") \u2192 back in `nfs_lookup_revalidate` at line 1155-1156: `nfs_check_verifier` returns 0 \u2192 falls through to full lookup \u2192 same path\n\nIn all cases, -ERESTARTSYS causes `nfs_lookup_revalidate` to return 0 (dentry invalid) instead of returning the error.\n\nBut is this actually the bug? Let me check - if `d_revalidate` returns 0 (invalid), VFS will just redo the lookup. If the SIGKILL is cleared by then, the redo would succeed. The problem would be if the SIGKILL makes every subsequent lookup fail too.\n\nActually, if the process has SIGKILL pending, it won't be able to complete any NFS operation that sleeps with TASK_KILLABLE. So every attempt to revalidate will fail, and the VFS will keep seeing the dentry as invalid.\n\nBut if the process is being killed (SIGKILL pending), why would it matter if the NFS operation fails? The process is going to die anyway.\n\nThe scenario might be:\n1. User process receives SIGKILL (e.g., OOM killer kills it)\n2. Before dying, kernel tries to do cleanup (e.g., closing files, releasing references)\n3. During cleanup, kernel needs to revalidate NFS inode\n4. NFS getattr fails with -ERESTARTSYS\n5. NFS dentry is invalidated\n6. Other processes (which DON'T have SIGKILL) now see the NFS path as invalid\n\nBut wait - other processes would have fresh dentries or would do their own `d_revalidate` which would succeed since they don't have SIGKILL pending.\n\nHmm, unless the issue is that the autofs4 expire daemon process has SIGKILL pending (because it's been sent SIGKILL to restart) while it's checking if a mount is busy by following paths through NFS. But autofs4_expire_direct/indirect doesn't follow through the NFS path, it just checks mount reference counts.\n\nActually, let me re-read the bug description more carefully: \"Root NFS + autofs setup where getattr reply is received by server but client returns -ERESTARTSYS instead of processing it.\"\n\nThis is really specific - \"getattr reply is received by server\" means the server DID send the reply. The client sent the request, the server processed it and sent the reply, but the client returned -ERESTARTSYS before the reply was processed.\n\nThis means the timeline is:\n1. Client sends GETATTR request\n2. Client starts waiting for response  \n3. SIGKILL arrives at client while waiting\n4. `rpc_wait_bit_killable` returns -ERESTARTSYS (without waiting for reply)\n5. Server processes request and sends reply\n6. Client has already removed request from `xprt->recv` (via `xprt_release`)\n7. Server reply arrives but XID not found - reply discarded\n8. GETATTR returns -ERESTARTSYS to caller\n\nThe question is WHY SIGKILL arrives while this particular process is waiting for NFS GETATTR. This must be something about the autofs + root NFS interaction in 4.1.\n\nLet me look at what function the automount process runs when it's triggered by autofs. In the user description, it says \"autofs\" is involved. The automount daemon is a userspace daemon. When the kernel wants to trigger a mount, it writes to the autofs pipe. The automountd daemon reads the pipe, does the mount, then signals the kernel.\n\nWhen the automountd daemon dies (receives SIGKILL), `autofs4_catatonic_mode` is called. But before dying, the daemon might try to clean up mounts. During cleanup, the daemon might try to do stat() on NFS paths.\n\nActually, here's another angle: what if the automountd process itself IS dying with SIGKILL, and while dying, it's doing cleanup that involves NFS path lookups?\n\nBut the user said this is a regression from 3.14 to 4.1. So something changed in the kernel between these versions.\n\nLet me think about what could have changed:\n1. Addition of `AUTOFS_INF_NO_RCU` flag and the associated RCU synchronization in `autofs4_expire_direct` (line 318-330)\n2. Changes to how signals are handled in RPC layer\n3. Changes to NFS error handling (how -ERESTARTSYS propagates)\n4. Changes to d_revalidate called context\n\nActually, looking at lines 317-330 of `autofs4_expire_direct`:\n```c\nif (!autofs4_direct_busy(mnt, root, timeout, do_now)) {\n    ino->flags |= AUTOFS_INF_NO_RCU;\n    spin_unlock(&sbi->fs_lock);\n    synchronize_rcu();\n    spin_lock(&sbi->fs_lock);\n    if (!autofs4_direct_busy(mnt, root, timeout, do_now)) {\n        ino->flags |= AUTOFS_INF_EXPIRING;\n        smp_mb();\n        ino->flags &= ~AUTOFS_INF_NO_RCU;\n        init_completion(&ino->expire_complete);\n        spin_unlock(&sbi->fs_lock);\n        return root;\n    }\n    ino->flags &= ~AUTOFS_INF_NO_RCU;\n}\n```\n\nThe `AUTOFS_INF_NO_RCU` flag check in `autofs4_expire_wait` at line 497:\n```c\nif (!(ino->flags & (AUTOFS_INF_EXPIRING | AUTOFS_INF_NO_RCU)))\n    return 0;\nif (rcu_walk)\n    return -ECHILD;\n```\n\nThis `AUTOFS_INF_NO_RCU` flag is checked in `autofs4_expire_wait`. If set, it forces non-RCU path revalidation. This might be new in 4.1 (checking NO_RCU flag in expire_wait).\n\nActually, you know what - let me look at this very differently.
